- `doctrine:when-the-Light-of-the-world-died-the-world-went-dark-enough-to-feel` —["thick darkness... the inhabitants who had not fallen could feel the vapor of darkness" — no candle, torch, or fire could be kindled — "for the space of three days"; the plague of Egypt's "darkness which may be felt" now fallen, lasting the exact span Christ lay in the tomb; when the Light of the World died the world went literally, palpably dark — a three-day parable of what the world is without Christ]→ 8:20-23 (Ex 10:21-23; John 8:12; 1:4-5; 9:5)
- `theme:the-destruction-fulfills-Samuel's-sign-exactly` —[every detail of Samuel's death-prophecy (Hel 14:20-27) comes true: three hours of tempest and quaking, the rocks rent "in seams and in cracks," the cities sunk and burned and buried, three days of darkness; prophecy verified to the letter, the second great fulfillment after the birth-sign of ch 1]→ 8:5-23 (Hel 14:20-27; 1 Ne 19:10-12; 3 Ne 1:20)
- `theme:the-too-late-repentance-the-recognition-that-comes-when-it-can-no-longer-save` —["O that we had repented before this great and terrible day... and had not killed and stoned the prophets... then would our mothers and our fair daughters, and our children have been spared"; repentance finally come, too late to save those it loved — the awful clarity arriving when it can no longer change anything (Hel 13:38's "everlastingly too late" fulfilled); and they lament not their own danger but the cost to others — delayed repentance is never only about the self]→ 8:24-25 (Hel 13:38; Alma 34:33-35; Prov 1:24-31)

### from 3 Nephi 9
- `doctrine:the-same-voice-pronounces-the-wo-and-extends-the-arm-of-mercy` —[the voice that says "Wo, wo, wo" and recounts the burned cities turns without a pause to "will ye not now return unto me... that I may heal you?... mine arm of mercy is extended towards you"; judge and healer are one Person, the turn instantaneous, mercy the final and longer word — He speaks in the darkness, and the first thing the survivors hear is not "you deserved this" but the offer of healing]→ 9:2-14 (Isa 54:7-8; Hab 3:2; Hosea 11:8-9; 3 Ne 18:32)
- `doctrine:Christ's-full-divinity-declared-in-his-own-voice` —["I am Jesus Christ the Son of God. I created the heavens and the earth... I was with the Father from the beginning. I am in the Father, and the Father in me... I am the light and the life of the world. I am Alpha and Omega"; the most comprehensive divinity declaration in the book, spoken by Christ Himself out of the darkness after His resurrection — Creator, eternal, one with the Father, light and life, beginning and end]→ 9:15-18 (John 1:1-14; Col 1:16; Heb 1:2-3; Rev 1:8; Mosiah 15:1-5)
- `doctrine:the-broken-heart-and-contrite-spirit-replace-animal-sacrifice` —["your sacrifices and your burnt offerings shall be done away... ye shall offer for a sacrifice unto me a broken heart and a contrite spirit"; the Lamb having been slain, the outward blood-sacrifice that pointed to Him is fulfilled and replaced by the inward one — sacrifice was never about the animal but always about the surrendered heart, broken of its pride]→ 9:19-20 (Ps 51:16-17; Mosiah 13:27-31; Heb 10:1-14; D&C 59:8)
- `doctrine:the-baptism-of-fire-can-come-unfelt` —["whoso cometh unto me with a broken heart and a contrite spirit, him will I baptize with fire and with the Holy Ghost, even as the Lamanites... were baptized with fire and with the Holy Ghost, and they knew it not"; the fire comes to the broken heart and can come so gently you only recognize it in retrospect — not always a dramatic burning but sometimes a quiet filling, unfelt in the moment]→ 9:20 (Hel 5:45; Acts 2:1-4; 2 Ne 31:13-14)
- `doctrine:come-as-a-little-child` —["whoso repenteth and cometh unto me as a little child, him will I receive, for of such is the kingdom of God"; after the cosmic divinity claims and the convulsed earth, the way in is to come as a child — humility, trust, teachability; the Creator of heaven and earth asks to be approached the way a child approaches a parent]→ 9:22 (Mark 10:15; 3 Ne 11:37-38; Mosiah 3:19)
- `theme:the-Creator-came-to-his-own-and-was-rejected-by-what-he-made` —["I created the heavens and the earth... I came unto my own, and my own received me not"; the vastness of the divinity claim and the humility of the rejection in adjacent verses — the God who made all things came to His own creation and was crucified by the creatures He made, submitting to be slain by what He made to redeem it; the contrast is the gospel]→ 9:15-16 (John 1:3, 11; Isa 53:3; Phil 2:5-8)

### from 3 Nephi 10
- `doctrine:the-hen-gathering-her-chickens-the-tenderest-image-of-Christ` —["how oft have I gathered you as a hen gathereth her chickens under her wings, and have nourished you"; the Creator of heaven and earth pictures His love not as eagle or lion but as a hen — the humblest protective creature, who in a fire covers her chicks with her own wings rather than leave them exposed; to be gathered to Christ is to run under the wing, into the warmth, covered by Him, exactly when the danger is greatest]→ 10:4-6 (Matt 23:37; Luke 13:34; Ps 91:4; Deut 32:11)
- `doctrine:the-three-tenses-of-Christ's-gathering` —["how oft HAVE I gathered you... how oft WOULD I have gathered you, and ye would not... how oft WILL I gather you, if ye will repent"; the grammar holds the whole drama of salvation — the gathering He has always done, the gathering they refused, the gathering still on offer; the wings are still spread, even after the destruction, for any who will come]→ 10:4-6 (Matt 23:37; 3 Ne 9:13-14; D&C 43:24-25)
- `doctrine:ye-would-not-the-willingness-of-Christ-defeated-only-by-the-human-refusal` —["how oft would I have gathered you... and ye would not"; the destruction was never God's failure to gather but the people's refusal to be gathered — the hen spread her wings, the chicks would not run beneath them; God's desire to save is total and unwearying, and the only thing that defeats it is the human "would not"; the whole of human tragedy in two words]→ 10:5 (Ezek 18:32; 33:11; 2 Pet 3:9; 1 Tim 2:4)
- `theme:mourning-turned-into-joy-the-third-day-morning` —[the three days end, "the earth did cleave together again, that it stood; and... their mourning was turned into joy, and their lamentations into the praise and thanksgiving unto the Lord Jesus Christ, their Redeemer"; the darkness lifts on the third-day morning when He rises — the rent earth cleaves together at the resurrection, and the survivors' grief becomes worship of the Redeemer who spoke in the worst of it]→ 10:9-10 (Ps 30:5, 11; Isa 61:3; John 16:20; 3 Ne 8:18)
- `theme:the-spared-are-those-who-received-the-prophets` —["it was the more righteous part of the people who were saved, and it was they who received the prophets and stoned them not... who had not shed the blood of the saints"; the criterion of preservation was how they treated the truth-tellers — the prophet-rejection thread resolving in the simplest measure of a people's standing]→ 10:12 (3 Ne 9:13; 2 Ne 26:8; Matt 10:40-41)
- `theme:the-promise-of-the-descent` —["soon after the ascension of Christ into heaven he did truly manifest himself unto them — Showing his body unto them, and ministering unto them"; the voice in the darkness was the prelude — now He will come in person, the hen who called from heaven descending to walk among the chicks; everything from the birth-signs through the destruction to the voice has cleared the ground for this]→ 10:18-19 (3 Ne 11:8-15; Acts 1:9-11; John 20:27)

### from 3 Nephi 11
- `doctrine:the-Father-always-points-to-the-Son-hear-ye-him` —["Behold my Beloved Son, in whom I am well pleased, in whom I have glorified my name—hear ye him"; the same words as the baptism, the Transfiguration, and the First Vision — every time the Father speaks audibly He directs all attention to the Son; His consistent message is not "look at me" but "hear ye him"]→ 11:7 (Matt 3:17; 17:5; JS–H 1:17; John 12:28)
- `doctrine:the-still-small-voice-understood-only-when-the-hearer-attunes` —["it being a small voice it did pierce them to the very soul, and did cause their hearts to burn"; but they "understood it not" the first two times — only "the third time they did open their ears... and did look steadfastly towards heaven" and then understood; the voice was speaking the whole time, what changed was the hearers; revelation requires the receiver to quiet down, turn toward the source, attend with the whole self]→ 11:3-6 (1 Kgs 19:11-13; Hel 5:30; D&C 85:6; Luke 24:32)
- `doctrine:the-resurrected-Christ-keeps-the-wounds-the-marks-of-the-Atonement-are-eternal` —["that ye may feel the prints of the nails in my hands and in my feet, that ye may know that I am the God of Israel... and have been slain for the sins of the world"; the risen, glorified body keeps the wounds — His permanent identification; the Atonement is written into His immortal flesh forever, the one thing He carried out of the tomb; the marks declare both His divinity and His suffering at once]→ 11:14-15 (John 20:24-29; Isa 49:16; Zech 13:6; D&C 6:37)
- `doctrine:Christ-meets-souls-one-by-one-not-as-a-mass` —[the multitude "went forth... going forth one by one until they had all gone forth, and did see with their eyes and did feel with their hands"; 2,500 people, each individually, while the risen Lord stood and let every one put their hands in His side; He relates to souls not as a faceless crowd but as individuals to be met, each given their own undeniable witness, each known — the patience and condescension of it]→ 11:15 (3 Ne 17:25; Luke 15:4-7; John 10:3, 14; Isa 43:1)
- `doctrine:contention-is-of-the-devil-the-father-of-contention` —["he that hath the spirit of contention is not of me, but is of the devil, who is the father of contention, and he stirreth up the hearts of men to contend with anger"; the risen Christ's FIRST doctrinal concern targets not the content of disputes but the spirit of contention itself — even disputing "concerning the points of my doctrine" can be the devil's work if done in that spirit; the spirit in which I hold the truth matters as much as the truth]→ 11:28-30 (2 Tim 2:23-24; 1 Cor 1:10-13; Eph 4:31-32; James 3:14-18)
- `doctrine:the-doctrine-of-Christ-the-rock-believe-repent-be-baptized-become-as-a-child` —["the Father commandeth all men, everywhere, to repent and believe in me... ye must repent, and become as a little child, and be baptized in my name... whoso buildeth upon this buildeth upon my rock, and the gates of hell shall not prevail against them"; the pure gospel given by Christ Himself, witnessed by the whole Godhead — stunningly simple: faith, repentance, baptism, the Holy Ghost, the childlike heart; that's the whole rock]→ 11:31-39 (2 Ne 31:2-21; Matt 7:24-27; 3 Ne 27:13-21; Mark 10:15)
- `doctrine:declare-more-or-less-than-the-doctrine-and-it-comes-of-evil` —["whoso shall declare more or less than this, and establish it for my doctrine, the same cometh of evil... buildeth upon a sandy foundation"; neither to be added to nor subtracted from — both addition (complicating) and subtraction (diluting) come of evil and miss the rock; the gospel's power is in its simplicity]→ 11:40 (Rev 22:18-19; Deut 4:2; Gal 1:8-9; 2 Ne 28:30)
- `doctrine:the-Godhead-are-one` —["the Father, and the Son, and the Holy Ghost are one; and I am in the Father, and the Father in me, and the Father and I are one"; the unity of the Godhead, witnessed in the threefold record — central to the divinity question]→ 11:27, 36 (Mosiah 15:1-5; Alma 11:44; John 17:21-22; 3 Ne 9:15)

### from 3 Nephi 12
- `doctrine:the-Beatitudes-are-wrapped-in-the-doctrine-of-Christ` —[the Nephite Beatitudes framed front and back by the doctrine of Christ: "blessed are ye if ye shall believe in me and be baptized... baptize you with fire and with the Holy Ghost"; and altered — "poor in spirit WHO COME UNTO ME," "filled WITH THE HOLY GHOST"; blessings flow from coming to Christ and receiving His Spirit, not generic virtue — descriptions of what a soul becomes in conversion]→ 12:1-6 (3 Ne 11:31-39; 9:20; Matt 5:3-12)
- `doctrine:more-blessed-are-they-who-believe-the-witnesses-words-without-seeing` —["more blessed are they who shall believe in your words because that ye shall testify that ye have seen me"; a special blessing on those who'd believe the witnesses without seeing — the Nephite parallel to "blessed are they that have not seen, and yet have believed," pointed at every future reader; the faith on testimony not sight is the MORE blessed one, the record made for this blessing]→ 12:2 (John 20:29; 1 Pet 1:8; Ether 12:6; Morm 9:25)
- `doctrine:the-law-is-now-fulfilled-old-things-done-away-all-things-new` —[Matthew's "till all be fulfilled" (future) becomes "in me it hath all been fulfilled"; and "those things which were of old time, which were under the law, in me are all fulfilled. Old things are done away, and all things have become new"; spoken after the cross, the law already done away, replaced by the broken heart — the great transition accomplished]→ 12:18, 46-47 (Heb 8:13; 2 Cor 5:17; Jer 31:31-33; 3 Ne 9:17)
- `doctrine:the-higher-law-governs-the-heart-not-just-the-act` —[each old commandment driven inward: not just "thou shalt not kill" but "whosoever is angry"; not just no adultery but no lust; not just an eye for an eye but turn the other cheek; not just love your neighbor but love your enemy; the law of Moses governed behavior, the higher law governs the heart — Christ wants not clean hands but a clean heart, every commandment pushed to the inward source]→ 12:21-44 (Matt 5:21-44; Ezek 36:26; Jer 31:33; 1 Sam 16:7)
- `doctrine:the-higher-law-on-anger-comes-right-after-contention-named-as-of-the-devil` —["whosoever is angry with his brother shall be in danger of his judgment" — the Nephite version omitting "without a cause," making it starker: anger itself, not just unjustified anger; coming right after the risen Christ named the spirit of contention "of the devil" (11:29); the higher law forbids the anger that is murder's seed]→ 12:22 (3 Ne 11:28-30; Eph 4:26-32; James 1:19-20; Matt 5:22)
- `doctrine:be-perfect-even-as-I-the-resurrected-Christ-adds-himself-as-the-standard` —["I would that ye should be perfect even as I, or your Father who is in heaven is perfect"; Matthew said only "even as your Father" because Christ was not yet perfected through death — here, risen and glorified, He adds "even as I," now the completed exemplar; "perfect" (teleios) is wholeness/completion, not flawlessness — be made complete even as I am, the destination of the whole Sermon]→ 12:48 (Matt 5:48; 3 Ne 19:29; 27:27; Moro 10:32-33)
- `theme:salt-and-light-as-gift-and-commission` —["I give unto you to be the salt of the earth... the light of this people"; the Nephite version a conferral not just a description (KJV "ye are") — Christ confers the identity, the disciples made salt and light and called not to lose savor nor hide the light, "that they may see your good works and glorify your Father"]→ 12:13-16 (Matt 5:13-16; D&C 101:39-40; Philip 2:15)

### from 3 Nephi 13
- `doctrine:they-have-their-reward-the-human-applause-is-the-hypocrite's-full-wage` —[three times — alms, prayer, fasting — "they have their reward"; not no reward but THEIRS, the human applause they were after; they spent their righteousness to purchase admiration and got exactly what they paid for, nothing left for heaven; two audiences and two paymasters — do it for people and people's notice is your full wage, do it in secret and God Himself becomes the rewarder]→ 13:2, 5, 16 (Matt 6:2-18; D&C 121:34-37; John 12:43)
- `doctrine:where-your-treasure-is-there-will-your-heart-be-the-heart-follows-the-treasure` —["for where your treasure is, there will your heart be also"; the heart FOLLOWS the treasure, not the reverse — a diagnostic (to find your heart, look where your time/money/attention go) and a tool (you can move your heart by moving your treasure; lay up treasure in heaven and the heart relocates there); the bright inverse of Hel 13's slippery treasures]→ 13:19-21 (Matt 6:19-21; Hel 13:21-37; Luke 12:33-34)
- `doctrine:the-single-eye-and-the-two-masters-undivided-devotion` —["if thine eye be single, thy whole body shall be full of light... No man can serve two masters... Ye cannot serve God and Mammon"; the eye fixed singly on God's glory fills the body with light, the divided gaze with darkness; divided allegiance is impossible, healed only by a single priority]→ 13:22-24 (D&C 88:67; Alma 5:39-42; 1 Kgs 18:21; James 1:8)
- `doctrine:take-no-thought-is-the-charge-to-the-called-twelve-not-blanket-counsel` —["when Jesus had spoken these words he looked upon the twelve whom he had chosen, and said unto them... ye are they whom I have chosen to minister... Therefore I say unto you, take no thought for your life"; the Nephite version makes explicit what's ambiguous in Matthew — "take no thought" is spoken TO THE TWELVE as the charge of consecration, the trust full-time ministry requires of those who've left their livelihoods; not a blanket prohibition on prudence for every disciple but the specific faith of the sent]→ 13:25-34 (Matt 6:25-34; D&C 84:79-85; Alma 31:37; Luke 10:4-7)
- `doctrine:seek-ye-first-the-kingdom-and-all-these-things-shall-be-added` —["seek ye first the kingdom of God and his righteousness, and all these things shall be added unto you"; the principle that does generalize — the temporal needs are real and the Father knows them, but seek the kingdom FIRST and the rest is added; the anxiety dissolved not by securing the temporal first but by putting the kingdom first and trusting God to add the rest]→ 13:33 (Matt 6:33; Luke 12:31; Hag 1:2-11; D&C 88:67)
- `doctrine:forgiveness-is-conditioned-on-our-forgiving` —["if ye forgive men their trespasses your heavenly Father will also forgive you; but if ye forgive not... neither will your Father forgive your trespasses"; the one petition of the Lord's Prayer Christ expands — our forgiveness conditioned on our forgiving; the measure we give is the measure we receive]→ 13:14-15 (Matt 6:14-15; 18:23-35; Mosiah 26:31; Mark 11:25)

### from 3 Nephi 14
- `doctrine:cast-the-beam-from-your-own-eye-first-then-help-your-brother` —["first cast the beam out of thine own eye; and then shalt thou see clearly to cast the mote out of thy brother's eye"; not a blanket prohibition on discernment but a sequence — the goal is still to help, but self-correction first because the beam distorts your vision; correction is sequenced not forbidden, and what follows comes from humility instead of hypocrisy]→ 14:1-5 (John 8:7; Rom 2:1-3; Gal 6:1; Matt 7:1-5)
- `doctrine:the-Father-gives-good-gifts-lesser-to-greater` —["if ye then, being evil, know how to give good gifts unto your children, how much more shall your Father who is in heaven give good things to them that ask him?"; even flawed parents give bread not a stone, and that instinct is a faint fallen echo of God's infinitely greater desire; asking is not pleading with a reluctant deity but a child asking a Father who already wants to give]→ 14:7-11 (Luke 11:9-13; James 1:17; Matt 7:7-11)
- `doctrine:the-golden-rule-is-the-law-and-the-prophets-stated-actively` —["all things whatsoever ye would that men should do to you, do ye even so to them, for this is the law and the prophets"; stated actively (do to others) not negatively (don't do) — not enough to avoid harm, I'm to actively do the good I'd want; the entire moral content of scripture in one operational rule]→ 14:12 (Matt 7:12; Lev 19:18; Rom 13:8-10)
- `doctrine:the-strait-gate-the-narrow-way-the-few` —["strait is the gate, and narrow is the way, which leadeth unto life, and few there be that find it"; salvation is not the default or majority path — the broad road has many, the narrow way few; it requires deliberately entering the strait gate, not drifting]→ 14:13-14 (2 Ne 31:17-21; 9:41; 1 Ne 8:20; Luke 13:24)
- `doctrine:by-their-fruits-ye-shall-know-them` —["ye shall know them by their fruits... a good tree cannot bring forth evil fruit"; the test of anything claiming to be of God is not appearance, words, or credentials but fruit — the wolf wears sheep's clothing, the test that cuts through is what it actually produces; watch the fruit, not the foliage]→ 14:15-20 (Moro 7:5-17; Alma 32:42; Matt 12:33; Luke 6:43-45)
- `doctrine:I-never-knew-you-salvation-is-relational-not-the-works-resume` —["have we not prophesied in thy name... cast out devils... done many wonderful works? And then will I profess unto them: I never knew you"; they prophesied and worked miracles IN HIS NAME, and He says "I never knew you"; what saves is not what I accomplish for Christ but whether Christ KNOWS me, the surrendered heart that does the Father's will; salvation is relational not transactional, the most frightening sentence spoken to the religiously accomplished]→ 14:21-23 (Mosiah 5:13; 26:24-27; Matt 25:12; D&C 112:26)
- `doctrine:the-house-on-the-rock-is-hearing-AND-doing` —["whoso heareth these sayings of mine AND DOETH them" the wise builder; "heareth... and doeth them not" the foolish — both heard, the difference is doing; the storm beats both houses identically (as Hel 5:12), the foundation determines only whether it stands; the Sermon's final word — to hear it and not do it is to build the whole discourse on sand]→ 14:24-27 (Hel 5:12; 3 Ne 11:39-40; Matt 7:24-27; James 1:22-25)

### from 3 Nephi 15
- `doctrine:I-am-he-that-gave-the-law-Christ-is-Jehovah` —["I am he that gave the law, and I am he who covenanted with my people Israel"; the risen Christ identifies Himself as the God who gave the law at Sinai and covenanted with ancient Israel — Jehovah, the LORD of the OT (footnote: "Jesus Christ, Jehovah"); the God of the burning bush is the God of the manger and the cross; the OT God of law and NT Christ of grace are the same Being]→ 15:5 (1 Cor 10:1-4; Ex 3:14; Mosiah 13:33-34; 3 Ne 11:14)
- `doctrine:the-law-of-Moses-ended-in-Christ-but-the-covenant-continues` —["the law in me is fulfilled... it hath an end," yet "the covenant which I have made with my people is not all fulfilled"; a precise distinction — the law (performances pointing to His sacrifice) ended, but the covenant (the gathering, things to come) still stands; the temporary schoolmaster done, the enduring relationship continuing]→ 15:4-8 (Heb 8:6-13; Gal 3:23-25; 2 Ne 25:24-27)
- `doctrine:I-am-the-law-the-law-replaced-by-a-Person-look-unto-me` —["Behold, I am the law, and the light. Look unto me, and endure to the end, and ye shall live"; the law replaced by a Person — the whole point of the law was to bring people to Him, so the pointer gives way to the thing it pointed at; "look unto me" (the brazen-serpent gaze) replaces "keep the statutes"; religion shifts from rule-keeping to relationship]→ 15:9 (John 14:6; 2 Ne 26:1; 3 Ne 9:18; Col 3:11)
- `doctrine:other-sheep-one-fold-one-shepherd-the-flock-spans-the-earth` —["ye are they of whom I said: Other sheep I have which are not of this fold... there shall be one fold, and one shepherd"; the Jews thought it meant the Gentiles, but the other sheep were the Nephites and the lost tribes; the Shepherd's flock spans the whole earth under one Lord who personally visits each portion, until all are one fold]→ 15:17, 21-24 (John 10:16; Ezek 34:11-23; 1 Ne 22:3-4; 3 Ne 16:1-4)
- `theme:Christ-came-in-person-to-the-other-sheep-they-were-not-second-class` —["ye have both heard my voice, and seen me; and ye are my sheep"; He didn't delegate the Nephites to a lesser revelation but descended and let them touch His wounds, exactly as at Jerusalem — the scattered, whom the proud center forgot, were never forgotten by the Shepherd]→ 15:24 (3 Ne 11:14-15; John 10:14, 27; Isa 49:15-16)
- `theme:iniquity-shrinks-the-capacity-to-receive-truth` —["because of stiffneckedness and unbelief they understood not my word; therefore I was commanded to say no more of the Father concerning this thing unto them"; the unbelieving heart can't be told certain things — not because God withholds arbitrarily but because the hardened heart cannot hold them (John 16:12); iniquity shrinks the capacity to receive — Jerusalem made itself unable to hear about the other sheep]→ 15:18 (John 16:12; D&C 10:59; 1 Cor 3:1-2)
- `theme:Israel-separated-because-of-iniquity-judgment-and-preservation-in-one-act` —["ye were separated from among them because of their iniquity; therefore it is because of their iniquity that they know not of you"; the scattering was both a judgment on the unfaithful and a providential preservation of the faithful elsewhere — Lehi's family led away because of Jerusalem's iniquity, a rescue from one angle and a consequence from another]→ 15:19-20 (1 Ne 17:35-38; 2 Ne 1:5-11; Jer 24:5-7)

### from 3 Nephi 16
- `doctrine:the-record-made-for-the-Gentiles-to-reach-the-remnant` —["I command you that ye shall write these sayings... that these sayings shall be kept and shall be manifested unto the Gentiles, that through the fulness of the Gentiles, the remnant of their seed... may be brought to a knowledge of me, their Redeemer"; the Book of Mormon names its own purpose in Christ's mouth — written now, brought forth to the Gentiles in the latter days, and through them to the scattered remnant; a covenant instrument with a destination beyond its reader]→ 16:4 (2 Ne 25:18; 30:3; 1 Ne 13:39-42; Morm 5:15)
- `doctrine:the-gospel-comes-to-the-Gentiles-first-in-the-latter-days` —["because of their belief in me... and because of the unbelief of you, O house of Israel, in the latter day shall the truth come unto the Gentiles"; the order reversed — Israel-first in antiquity, Gentiles-first in the last days; Paul's Romans 11 mystery, the Gentiles grafted in first so they can serve Israel's gathering]→ 16:6-7 (Rom 11:11-25; Jacob 5:60-68; 1 Ne 13:42)
- `doctrine:the-fulness-can-be-taken-away-if-the-Gentiles-reject-it-in-pride` —["at that day when the Gentiles shall sin against my gospel... and shall be lifted up in the pride of their hearts above all nations... filled with all manner of lyings... priestcrafts, and whoredoms, and of secret abominations... I will bring the fulness of my gospel from among them"; the privilege of the fulness first carries the gravest exposure — it can be taken away; the litany reads as a contemporary indictment; a warning to the heirs not outsiders — pride forfeits it, "salt that hath lost its savor"]→ 16:10-15 (Morm 8:31-41; 2 Ne 28:12-32; D&C 1:14-16; 3 Ne 12:13)
- `doctrine:the-repentant-Gentiles-are-numbered-among-Israel` —["if the Gentiles will repent and return unto me... behold they shall be numbered among my people, O house of Israel"; the door stays open — repent and the Gentile is grafted permanently into Israel; covenant by adoption; the warning is a mercy, telling them in advance how they could lose what they were given]→ 16:13 (Gal 3:7, 29; 1 Ne 14:1-2; Abr 2:9-11)
- `theme:contention-healed-in-Zion-the-watchmen-see-eye-to-eye` —["Thy watchmen shall lift up the voice; with the voice together shall they sing, for they shall see eye to eye when the Lord shall bring again Zion"; where once watchmen cried warnings into hostile cities, in Zion they sing together and "see eye to eye" (perfect agreement); the contention named "of the devil" (11:29) finally healed — one voice singing in unity]→ 16:18 (Isa 52:8; 3 Ne 11:29; Zeph 3:9; Eph 4:13)
- `theme:the-gathering-ends-in-a-song-not-a-judgment` —["Break forth into joy, sing together, ye waste places of Jerusalem... The Lord hath made bare his holy arm in the eyes of all the nations; and all the ends of the earth shall see the salvation of God"; even the ruins commanded to sing — the whole arc of scattering, warning, and gathering ends not in judgment but in joy, God baring His arm so visibly all the earth sees His salvation]→ 16:18-20 (Isa 52:9-10; 3 Ne 20:34-35; Ps 98:1-3)

### from 3 Nephi 17
- `doctrine:compassion-changed-His-plan-He-stayed-for-a-weeping-people` —[Christ announced His departure ("my time is at hand... I go... to show myself unto the lost tribes"), but "beheld they were in tears... as if they would ask him to tarry a little longer," and stayed: "my bowels are filled with compassion towards you"; the Lord let a weeping people's tears rewrite His plan — He stays for the ones who don't want Him to leave, and the longing to have Him tarry is itself something He answers]→ 17:1-7 (John 11:33-36; Luke 7:13; Matt 9:36; Mark 6:34)
- `doctrine:my-bowels-are-filled-with-compassion-the-visceral-love-that-acts` —["my bowels are filled with compassion towards you... filled with mercy"; the deepest idiom scripture has for love — the gut-level visceral tenderness, the same word used of the father running to the prodigal; and it acts: "Bring them hither... and I will heal them" — compassion that heals every one]→ 17:6-9 (Luke 15:20; Matt 14:14; Isa 63:15; Col 3:12)
- `doctrine:Christ-paces-His-teaching-to-our-capacity` —["I perceive that ye are weak, that ye cannot understand all my words... go ye unto your homes, and ponder... and prepare your minds for the morrow, and I come unto you again"; Christ gives what they can hold, sends them to ponder and pray, then returns with more — line upon line paced to the learner's weakness (John 16:12)]→ 17:2-3 (John 16:12; D&C 78:17-18; Mark 4:33; Isa 28:10)
- `doctrine:they-are-not-lost-unto-the-Father-nothing-is-lost-to-God` —["the lost tribes of Israel, for they are not lost unto the Father, for he knoweth whither he hath taken them"; the lost tribes are lost to us, not to God — what's lost to human knowledge is never lost to Him; applies to the tribes and to anything or anyone we've lost]→ 17:4 (Deut 4:31; Isa 49:15-16; Luke 12:6-7; Luke 15:4)
- `doctrine:the-prayer-that-cannot-be-written-the-boundary-of-language` —["the things which he prayed cannot be written... no tongue can speak, neither can there be written by any man, neither can the hearts of men conceive... no one can conceive of the joy which filled our souls at the time we heard him pray for us"; the abridger stops and says this cannot be written — heights of communion between Son and Father beyond human capacity; and the unspeakable joy was that the prayer was FOR them — to hear Christ intercede for you is a joy beyond conceiving]→ 17:14-17 (Isa 64:4; 1 Cor 2:9; Heb 7:25; Rom 8:34)
- `theme:Christ-wept-twice-from-fullness-not-grief` —[after "my joy is full," "he wept"; and after blessing the children, "he wept again"; tears of overflowing love and joy, not sorrow — the God who wept at Lazarus's tomb weeps here from fullness; the risen, glorified Christ is the most emotionally present being imaginable, weeping twice in a few verses — no stoic impassive deity]→ 17:20-22 (John 11:35; Luke 19:41; 3 Ne 17:14)
- `theme:the-children-are-the-climax-angels-of-fire-for-the-least` —[He blessed "their little children, one by one," then "Behold your little ones," and the heavens opened, "angels descending out of heaven as it were in the midst of fire... encircled those little ones about... and the angels did minister unto them"; the supreme miracle of the entire ministry given not to the leaders or the twelve but to the children — "of such is the kingdom" enacted in glory, the least honored above all, encircled with the same fire that protected Nephi and Lehi in prison]→ 17:21-24 (Matt 19:13-15; Mark 10:13-16; 3 Ne 11:37-38; Hel 5:23, 43-45)

### from 3 Nephi 18
- `doctrine:the-sacrament-always-remember-me-and-ye-shall-have-my-Spirit` —["this shall ye do in remembrance of my body... a testimony unto the Father that ye do always remember me. And if ye do always remember me ye shall have my Spirit to be with you"; the ordinance crystallizes the whole "remember, remember" theme (Hel 5) into an embodied weekly act — the antidote to the forgetting that destroys; the companionship of the Spirit tied to ALWAYS remembering]→ 18:7, 11 (Matt 26:26-29; Moro 4-5; Hel 5:9-12; D&C 20:75-79)
- `doctrine:watch-and-pray-always-Satan-desires-to-sift-you-as-wheat` —["ye must watch and pray always, lest ye be tempted by the devil... Satan desireth to have you, that he may sift you as wheat"; the same warning Christ gave Peter — the defense is not heroic resistance but constant prayer, because the adversary keeps no office hours so neither can the prayer; discipleship as a continuous watch]→ 18:15-18 (Luke 22:31-32; 1 Pet 5:8; D&C 10:22-27; Eph 6:18)
- `doctrine:I-am-the-light-which-ye-shall-hold-up-the-borrowed-light` —["hold up your light that it may shine unto the world. Behold I am the light which ye shall hold up—that which ye have seen me do"; the disciples don't generate the light, they hold up His — the moon not the sun; the job is not to dazzle with one's own goodness but to point past oneself to Christ; the failure mode is holding up myself instead of Him]→ 18:24 (Matt 5:14-16; 3 Ne 12:14; John 8:12; Hel 9:36)
- `doctrine:forbid-the-unworthy-from-the-sacrament-but-never-cast-out-the-person` —["ye shall not suffer any one knowingly to partake... unworthily... Nevertheless, ye shall not cast him out from among you, but ye shall minister unto him... for ye know not but what they will return and repent"; forbid the unworthy from the ORDINANCE, never cast them out of the FELLOWSHIP — the ordinance has a guard, the door has none; guards against both cheapening the sacrament and abandoning the sinner where they might be healed]→ 18:28-32 (1 Cor 11:27-29; 3 Ne 9:13; Matt 18:12-14; Gal 6:1)
- `doctrine:pray-in-your-families` —["Pray in your families unto the Father, always in my name, that your wives and your children may be blessed"; the watch is kept first in the home — the family that prays together is the family blessed and guarded]→ 18:21 (Alma 34:21; Deut 6:6-7; Josh 24:15)
- `theme:discipleship-is-a-continuous-posture-not-discrete-acts` —[the "always" recurs — always remember (v7), always pray (v15-19), always in my name; discipleship is a sustained watchfulness, remembering, and prayer, not religious moments punctuating a secular life — because the threat is sustained ("Satan desireth to have you," present tense)]→ 18:7-21 (1 Thes 5:17; Luke 18:1; D&C 93:49)
- `theme:the-commandments-are-the-cure-for-contention` —["I give you these commandments because of the disputations which have been among you. And blessed are ye if ye have no disputations"; the whole body of instruction given to treat the contention named "of the devil" (11:29); a church that does these things rightly has no need to dispute, the practices themselves embody the unity]→ 18:34 (3 Ne 11:28-30; 1 Cor 1:10; Eph 4:3)

### from 3 Nephi 19
- `doctrine:the-disciples-prayed-to-Jesus-as-their-Lord-and-their-God` —["they did pray unto Jesus, calling him their Lord and their God... they pray unto me because I am with them"; unusual — the standard is to pray to the Father in the Son's name, but with the Son bodily present they pray to Him and call Him God, and He receives it approvingly; one of the clearest affirmations of Christ's divinity and the propriety of worshiping Him]→ 19:18, 22 (3 Ne 9:15; 11:27; John 20:28; Rev 5:13-14)
- `doctrine:the-unity-prayer-believers-drawn-into-the-oneness-of-Father-and-Son` —["I pray... that I may be in them as thou, Father, art in me, that we may be one"; the oneness the believers are prayed into is the SAME oneness of the Father and the Son — not merely unity with each other but being drawn into the divine union; the telos of the gospel is union with God, the Godhead opening to receive the purified believer]→ 19:23, 29 (John 17:1-26; 1 Cor 6:17; D&C 35:2)
- `doctrine:purified-by-faith-Christ-glorified-in-the-believer` —["thou hast purified those whom I have chosen, because of their faith... that I may be in them as thou, Father, art in me, that we may be one, that I may be glorified in them"; the chain — faith → purification "in me" → oneness → Christ glorified IN the believer; the believer becoming the place where Christ's glory dwells]→ 19:28-29 (D&C 50:24-25; Moro 7:48; John 17:10; Col 1:27)
- `theme:the-disciples-made-white-as-Christ-transfiguration-glory-not-race` —["the light of his countenance did shine upon them, and behold they were as white as the countenance and also the garments of Jesus... they were white, even as Jesus"; the whiteness of GLORY — the transfiguring radiance of Christ's garments on the Mount, the luminosity of the sanctified, NOT complexion or race; purified by faith and drawn into the union, the disciples begin to look like Christ, made to shine by His face turned toward them]→ 19:25, 30 (Matt 17:1-2; Ex 34:29-35; Num 6:24-26; 3 Ne 17:24)
- `doctrine:the-prayer-beyond-words-understood-in-the-open-heart` —["tongue cannot speak the words which he prayed... nevertheless... their hearts were open and they did understand in their hearts the words which he prayed"; a deepening from ch 17 — the words could not be spoken or written, yet were understood directly in the heart; the deepest revelation bypasses language and is received heart-to-heart by the Spirit; the limit is on language, not understanding]→ 19:32-34 (1 Cor 2:9-14; 3 Ne 17:16-17; 2 Cor 12:4; Rom 8:26)
- `doctrine:faith-unlocks-miracles-unbelief-constrains-even-Christ` —["So great faith have I never seen among all the Jews; wherefore I could not show unto them so great miracles, because of their unbelief"; not "I chose not to" but "I COULD not" — the miracles required the receiving faith, and unbelief constrained what the Son of God could do (Mark 6:5-6); God's power flows in proportion to the faith that receives it; the despised remnant's greater faith unlocked what the first fold never saw — faith not lineage opens heaven]→ 19:35-36 (Mark 6:5-6; Matt 13:58; Ether 12:12; 2 Ne 27:23)
- `doctrine:Spirit-prompted-prayer-it-was-given-them-what-to-pray` —["they did not multiply many words, for it was given unto them what they should pray, and they were filled with desire"; prayer prompted by the Spirit — not vain repetition (13:7) but Spirit-given desire; the heart filled with desire and the words given, prayer "without ceasing" that needed no multiplying]→ 19:24 (Matt 6:7; Hel 10:5; D&C 46:30; Rom 8:26)

### from 3 Nephi 20
- `doctrine:the-miraculous-sacrament-the-bread-of-life-that-fills-the-soul-forever` —["there had been no bread... but he truly gave unto them... He that eateth this bread eateth of my body to his soul... his soul shall never hunger nor thirst, but shall be filled"; Christ provides the emblems Himself (the multiplied loaves), and the bread is not merely a symbol but the food of the soul — the bread of life (John 6:35), the means by which Christ becomes the soul's food and fills it forever; the people respond with worship]→ 20:3-9 (John 6:35, 48-58; Mark 6:41; 3 Ne 18:7)
- `doctrine:the-Father-and-I-are-one-appended-to-Isaiah` —[Christ quotes Isaiah 52:10 and ADDS "the salvation of the Father; and the Father and I are one"; the phrase is not in Isaiah — Christ appends His own commentary, affirming His oneness at the exact point Isaiah speaks of God's salvation; the salvation all the earth will see IS the Son's work, because the Father and Son are one]→ 20:35 (Isa 52:10; John 17:21-22; 3 Ne 9:15; 19:23)
- `doctrine:Christ-is-the-prophet-like-unto-Moses` —["I am he of whom Moses spake, saying: A prophet shall the Lord your God raise up... like unto me; him shall ye hear... and every soul who will not hear that prophet shall be cut off"; Christ applies Deut 18:15-19 to Himself — Moses gave the law, Christ fulfilled it; Moses led Israel from Egypt's bondage, Christ from sin's; Moses spoke with God, Christ IS God; to refuse Him is to be cut off]→ 20:23 (Deut 18:15-19; Acts 3:22-23; 1 Ne 22:20-21)
- `doctrine:the-blessing-of-Abraham's-seed-is-being-turned-from-iniquity` —["In thy seed shall all the kindreds of the earth be blessed... sent me to bless you in turning away every one of you from his iniquities"; the blessing of Abraham's seed is not prosperity or land but being TURNED FROM INIQUITY — the greatest blessing the covenant confers is repentance; "in thy seed shall all be blessed" means the turning of hearts from sin]→ 20:25-27 (Gen 12:3; 22:18; Gal 3:8; Abr 2:9-11)
- `doctrine:Israel-blessed-first-to-carry-the-blessing-to-all-kindreds` —[Christ came "unto you first" to bless by turning from iniquity, "and then... the pouring out of the Holy Ghost through me upon the Gentiles"; the covenant's purpose was never tribal privilege but the channel through which the blessing of repentance reaches "all the kindreds of the earth" — Israel blessed first not to hoard but to carry it to everyone]→ 20:26-27 (3 Ne 16:4; Rom 11:11-25; Gen 12:2-3)
- `theme:the-remnant-as-a-lion-and-the-New-Jerusalem` —["a remnant of the house of Jacob... as a lion among the beasts of the forest... this people will I establish in this land... a New Jerusalem. And the powers of heaven shall be in the midst... I will be in the midst of you"; the latter-day remnant restored as a lion among the unrepentant Gentiles (Micah 5:8), the American Zion with Christ in its midst]→ 20:16-22 (Micah 5:8-9; Gen 49:9; Isa 2:2-3; Ether 13:1-12)
- `theme:the-redemption-of-Zion-the-beautiful-feet-awake-be-clean` —["How beautiful upon the mountains are the feet of him that bringeth good tidings... that saith unto Zion: Thy God reigneth!... Awake, awake... put on thy strength, O Zion... be ye clean that bear the vessels of the Lord"; Isaiah 52's redemption of Zion — the messenger's beautiful feet, the city awaking in strength, the call to come out of Babylon and be clean, "redeemed without money," the marred-yet-cleansing servant]→ 20:32-45 (Isa 52:1-15; Mosiah 15:13-18; D&C 113:7-10)

### from 3 Nephi 21
- `doctrine:the-Book-of-Mormon's-coming-forth-is-the-sign-the-gathering-has-begun` —["I give unto you a sign, that ye may know the time... when these things which I declare unto you shall be made known unto the Gentiles... it shall be a sign unto them, that they may know that the work of the Father hath already commenced"; the sign is the very book in the reader's hands — its existence in the latter days IS the prophesied marker that the gathering of Israel has begun; the reader is not an observer of the prophecy but inside it, participating by reading it]→ 21:1-7 (1 Ne 10:14; Ether 4:17; D&C 20:8-11; Morm 5:12-15)
- `doctrine:a-free-nation-established-providentially-so-the-book-could-come-forth` —["it is wisdom in the Father that they should be established in this land, and be set up as a free people by the power of the Father, that these things might come forth"; the establishment of a free nation was providential, FOR bringing forth the book — the freedom instrumental to the covenant, which is why rejecting the gospel betrays the very purpose of the freedom]→ 21:4 (1 Ne 13:12-19; D&C 101:77-80; John 8:32)
- `doctrine:the-marred-but-preserved-servant-Gods-wisdom-greater-than-the-devils-cunning` —["the life of my servant shall be in my hand... although he shall be marred because of them. Yet I will heal him, for I will show unto them that my wisdom is greater than the cunning of the devil"; the servant who brings forth the book marred yet preserved until his work is done (echoing the suffering servant of Isa 52-53); the preservation proves divine wisdom overmatches satanic cunning — you may be marred, but if your life is in His hand you cannot be stopped till the work is done]→ 21:10 (2 Ne 3:6-15; Isa 52:13-14; D&C 135:1-3; Morm 8:16)
- `doctrine:the-two-Gentile-destinies-cut-off-or-numbered-among-Jacob` —[the unrepentant Gentiles' horses, chariots, strongholds, witchcrafts, images, "lyings, and deceivings... and whoredoms" all "cut off" and "done away" (Micah 5) — military power, false religion, social corruption dismantled; but the repentant "numbered among this the remnant of Jacob"; the same Gentiles who could be cut off can be grafted permanently into Israel by repentance]→ 21:14-22 (Micah 5:8-15; 3 Ne 16:14-15; Gal 3:29; 2 Ne 10:18-19)
- `theme:the-repentant-Gentiles-become-co-builders-of-the-New-Jerusalem` —["they shall come in unto the covenant... and they shall assist my people, the remnant of Jacob... that they may build a city, which shall be called the New Jerusalem"; the repentant Gentiles join the remnant not as second-class members but as co-builders of Zion — a reciprocity: the Gentiles brought the book to the remnant (the sign), now build Zion with them; "and I also will be in the midst"]→ 21:23-25 (Ether 13:1-12; 3 Ne 20:22; D&C 84:2-4; 3 Ne 16:13)
- `theme:the-gathering-of-all-the-dispersed-not-in-haste-God-before-and-behind` —["the work of the Father commence... among all the dispersed of my people, yea, even the tribes which have been lost... they shall not go out in haste, nor go by flight, for I will go before them... and I will be their rearward"; every scattered portion of Israel across all nations and centuries gathered home — not a panicked flight but an orderly homecoming with God going ahead and guarding the rear so none is lost]→ 21:26-29 (Isa 52:12; 3 Ne 20:42; D&C 133:24-35)

### from 3 Nephi 22 (Isaiah 54)
- `doctrine:for-a-small-moment-forsaken-with-everlasting-kindness-gathered-the-asymmetry` —["For a small moment have I forsaken thee, but with great mercies will I gather thee. In a little wrath I hid my face from thee for a moment, but with everlasting kindness will I have mercy on thee"; the whole comfort is the asymmetry — the affliction "a small moment," the mercy "everlasting"; not minimizing the pain but putting it in true proportion against the eternity of His kindness; whatever season of feeling forsaken, it is a small moment against everlasting kindness, and the gathering is the certain end]→ 22:7-8 (Isa 54:7-8; Ps 30:5; 2 Cor 4:17; D&C 121:7-8)
- `doctrine:the-covenant-of-peace-is-more-permanent-than-the-mountains` —["For the mountains shall depart and the hills be removed, but my kindness shall not depart from thee, neither shall the covenant of my peace be removed"; mountains are our image of permanence, and even they will dissolve before God's kindness departs — the covenant more enduring than the geology of the earth; bound to the oath after the flood, as sure as the sky after rain]→ 22:9-10 (Isa 54:9-10; Gen 9:11-16; Ps 94:14; Matt 24:35)
- `doctrine:God-is-Israel's-husband-the-covenant-as-marriage` —["thy maker, thy husband, the Lord of Hosts is his name... a woman forsaken and grieved in spirit, and a wife of youth, when thou wast refused"; God pictured not as master or king but as husband — the covenant is a marriage; the forsaking grieved as a wife abandoned, the reconciliation tender as a husband returning to the wife of his youth; God's relationship to His people is marital love]→ 22:5-6 (Isa 54:5-6; Hosea 2:19-20; Isa 62:4-5; Jer 3:14)
- `theme:the-barren-woman-who-sings-the-desolate-made-most-fruitful` —["Sing, O barren, thou that didst not bear... for more are the children of the desolate than the children of the married wife"; Israel/Zion as a barren woman commanded to sing before the children come, because she will have MORE than she who was never barren; the gospel's recurring reversal — the desolate made most fruitful — the command to sing while still barren, the promise sure enough to sing about in advance]→ 22:1-3 (Isa 54:1; Isa 49:21; 1 Sam 2:5; Gal 4:27)
- `doctrine:all-thy-children-shall-be-taught-of-the-Lord` —["all thy children shall be taught of the Lord; and great shall be the peace of thy children"; the new covenant of Jeremiah 31 — every child taught directly by God, knowing the Lord without intermediary; the peace that flows from being taught by God Himself]→ 22:13 (Isa 54:13; Jer 31:33-34; John 6:45; Isa 60:21)
- `doctrine:no-weapon-formed-against-thee-shall-prosper-righteousness-of-me` —["No weapon that is formed against thee shall prosper... This is the heritage of the servants of the Lord, and their righteousness is of me"; the protection of the covenant people — weapons formed but not prospering — and even the righteousness that protects them is God's gift, not their achievement, "of me"]→ 22:15-17 (Isa 54:17; 1 Ne 22:14-22; Rom 8:31; Phil 3:9)

### from 3 Nephi 23
- `doctrine:great-are-the-words-of-Isaiah-search-diligently` —["a commandment I give unto you that ye search these things diligently; for great are the words of Isaiah... all things that he spake have been and shall be"; Isaiah is the prophet most readers find hardest, and Christ's response to the difficulty is not "skip ahead" but "search diligently" — he's comprehensive (all Israel, the Gentiles, past/present/future), the difficulty being the texture of his greatness]→ 23:1-3 (2 Ne 25:1-8; Morm 8:23; Isa 49:6; Luke 24:27)
- `doctrine:Christ-audits-the-record-for-completeness-and-accuracy` —[having expounded all they had, Christ says "other scriptures I would that ye should write, that ye have not," asks for the record, "cast his eyes upon them," and identifies a specific omission; the resurrected Lord examined the scriptural record, found a fulfilled prophecy left out, and commanded it added — Christ Himself holds the record to completeness and accuracy, checking it against what actually happened; if the risen Lord audits His own scripture, verifying every claim against the source is participation in the standard Christ applied]→ 23:6-13 (3 Ne 8:1; W of M 1:11; 1 Ne 9:5; John 21:24)
- `doctrine:the-record-must-preserve-fulfillment-not-just-prophecy` —[what was omitted was a FULFILLED prophecy — Samuel said the saints would rise, they rose, and the fulfillment went unrecorded; Christ wants not just the prophecy but its vindication preserved, because the fulfilled word is itself a testimony (Hel 8:20-21); the dead rising at His rising is proof of His victory over death, and that proof belongs in the record]→ 23:9-13 (Matt 27:52-53; Hel 14:25; Hel 8:20-21; Deut 18:21-22)
- `theme:the-right-response-to-a-found-gap-is-acknowledge-and-correct` —["How be it that ye have not written this thing?... Nephi remembered that this thing had not been written... and Jesus commanded that it should be written"; the accountability is real but the response is not shame or self-justification — Nephi didn't defend the omission, he remembered, and it was written; the model for any stewardship of records or truth: high standard, real accountability, immediate correction of a found gap rather than "close enough"]→ 23:11-13 (Prov 28:13; 2 Cor 7:11; D&C 1:25-27)
- `doctrine:Christ-expounds-the-scriptures-in-one-then-the-disciples-teach` —[Christ "expounded all the scriptures in one... and commanded them that they should teach the things which he had expounded"; under His exposition the scattered prophecies become one coherent testimony (Luke 24:27) — the scriptures are not disconnected texts but, rightly expounded, "one" testimony of Him; and the interpretation is to be taught, not privately possessed — what the Lord opens to the disciples, they open to the people]→ 23:14 (Luke 24:27, 44; Matt 28:19-20; 3 Ne 18:36-37)

### from 3 Nephi 24 (Malachi 3)
- `doctrine:Christ-supplies-the-prophecy-the-Nephites-never-had` —[Malachi prophesied c. 430 BC, long after Lehi left Jerusalem c. 600 BC, so the brass plates couldn't contain him; Christ dictates the whole book word-for-word, "the words which the Father had given unto Malachi"; direct continuation of ch 23 — there He corrected an omission (fixing what was wrongly left out), here He supplies a prophecy never available (adding what couldn't be put in); the risen Lord curates His own scripture in both directions, line by line]→ 24:1 (3 Ne 23:6-13; Matt 11:10; D&C 45:9)
- `doctrine:Christ-the-messenger-of-the-covenant-came-suddenly-to-his-temple` —[the dramatic irony: Christ reads "the Lord, whom ye seek, shall suddenly come to his temple, even the messenger of the covenant" to a people gathered AT the temple in Bountiful (3 Ne 11:1), to whom He has just suddenly come — they live the fulfillment in the act of hearing the prophecy; yet it reaches forward to the Second Coming too, so the chapter holds both horizons: first coming (already, in mercy) and second (future, in fire)]→ 24:1 (3 Ne 11:1, 8-10; Mal 3:1; D&C 36:8)
- `doctrine:the-refiners-fire-purifies-not-only-punishes` —["who may abide the day of his coming?... he is like a refiner's fire... he shall sit as a refiner and purifier of silver... that they may offer an offering in righteousness"; the fire is severe but its object is purity, not ruin — the silversmith heats the ore to drive off the dross, watching until he sees his face in the metal; connects to ch 22's "small moment" affliction doing refining work; the same fire that consumes the dross purifies the silver — whether it destroys or refines depends on what there is in you to burn]→ 24:2-3 (3 Ne 25:1; Zech 13:9; 1 Cor 3:13; Mal 4:1)
- `doctrine:God-is-a-swift-witness-against-oppression-of-the-vulnerable` —[the swift-witness list sweeps from sorcery/adultery/false-oaths straight into economic and social sin — "those that oppress the hireling in his wages, the widow and the fatherless, and that turn aside the stranger"; God puts wage-theft and exploitation of the powerless in the same breath as the occult and sexual sins, all rooted in "fear not me"; the person who truly fears God does not cheat his workers or prey on widows, because he knows there is a Witness; my treatment of those with the least power over me is the truest measure of whether I fear God]→ 24:5 (Deut 24:14-15; Jas 1:27; Deut 10:18-19; Ps 94:6)
- `doctrine:God-changes-not-therefore-Jacob-is-not-consumed` —["For I am the Lord, I change not; therefore ye sons of Jacob are not consumed" — God's UNchangingness given as the reason His people are NOT destroyed; immutability is not the threat (an unbending God) but the floor (an unchanging covenant); the same God with every reason to consume a people gone away from His ordinances does not, BECAUSE He cannot stop being faithful; sits beside the refiner's fire on purpose — the One who refines will not change toward His people, so the fire is safe]→ 24:6 (Heb 13:8; Morm 9:9-11; 1 Ne 10:18; D&C 20:12)
- `doctrine:prove-me-now-herewith-the-one-invited-test-tithing` —["Will a man rob God?... In tithes and offerings... bring ye all the tithes into the storehouse... and prove me now herewith... if I will not open you the windows of heaven, and pour you out a blessing that there shall not be room enough to receive it"; the ONE place in scripture God invites being tested (everywhere else: "thou shalt not tempt the Lord"); the prosperity-covenant (1 Ne 2:20; 2 Ne 1:20) narrowed to tithing; "windows of heaven" inverts the flood (Gen 7:11) — windows that drowned the earth in judgment now pour blessing; robbing God curses the whole nation, giving opens the windows + rebukes the devourer]→ 24:8-12 (1 Ne 2:20; 2 Ne 1:20; D&C 64:23; Gen 7:11)
- `doctrine:God-keeps-a-book-of-remembrance-of-those-who-fear-him` —["a book of remembrance was written before him for them that feared the Lord, and that thought upon his name... they shall be mine... when I make up my jewels; and I will spare them as a man spareth his own son that serveth him"; stunning continuity with ch 23 — there Christ audits the EARTHLY record and requires it true; here God keeps a HEAVENLY record; the reason the earthly record must be accurate is that a heavenly record is kept with perfect accuracy; God Himself is a record-keeper, hearing the quiet conversations of the faithful and writing them down; the refined (v2) become the jewels (v17) become the spared son — one sequence, fire to tenderness]→ 24:16-18 (3 Ne 23:6-13; Moses 6:5-6; D&C 85:9; Ex 19:5; Dan 7:10)
- `theme:they-that-feared-the-Lord-spake-often-one-to-another` —[against the cynicism "it is vain to serve God... we call the proud happy" (vv14-15), a remnant "spake often one to another; and the Lord hearkened and heard"; God leans in and listens to the ordinary encouragement of those who fear Him when serving God feels vain — and writes it in the book of remembrance; the practice of mutual encouragement in the fear of the Lord is itself recorded by God]→ 24:16 (4 Ne 1:12; Moro 6:5-6; Heb 10:24-25)

### from 3 Nephi 25 (Malachi 4)
- `doctrine:one-day-two-destinies-the-same-fire-burns-and-heals` —[verses 1-2 describe the SAME day — "the day cometh that shall burn as an oven... all the proud... shall be stubble" / "unto you that fear my name shall the Son of Righteousness arise with healing in his wings"; not two days but one, great for one and dreadful for the other; direct continuation of ch 24's refiner's fire — the fire is constant, what differs is what there is in a person to burn; the proud reduced to ash, the faithful leaping like released calves; the day of the Lord is the great revealer, sorting all by one question: do you fear His name]→ 25:1-3 (3 Ne 24:2-3; Mal 3:2; 1 Cor 3:13; Ps 21:9)
- `doctrine:the-Son-of-Righteousness-arises-with-healing-in-his-wings` —[KJV "Sun of righteousness" (the dawn) → 3 Nephi "Son of Righteousness" (the title of Christ); the most consequential variant in the Malachi block, making explicit as a title what tradition read as image (the sol iustitiae, the dayspring of Luke 1:78); and the risen Son Himself reads the prophecy that names Himself, standing in the room where He'd just healed all their sick (3 Ne 17:7-9) — image and reality together; "wings" = kanaf, also the hem/border of the garment the bleeding woman touched for healing (Matt 9:20)]→ 25:2 (Mal 4:2; Luke 1:78; Matt 9:20-22; 3 Ne 17:7-9; Ether 9:22)
- `image:the-faithful-grow-up-as-calves-released-from-the-stall` —["ye shall go forth and grow up as calves in the stall" — penned calves with the door thrown open, bursting out leaping into the open field; the day that terrifies the wicked is, for those who fear God, the day the door opens and they run free; the sharpest contrast — the proud as ash under the soles of feet (v3), the faithful as released calves]→ 25:2-3 (1 Ne 22:24; Amos 6:4; Ps 30:11)
- `doctrine:remember-the-law-of-Moses-fulfilled-but-not-despised` —["Remember ye the law of Moses, my servant, which I commanded unto him in Horeb"; Christ had already declared the law fulfilled in Him (3 Ne 15:4-5), yet still reads them "remember" it — fulfilled is not despised; the schoolmaster that brought Israel to Christ (Gal 3:24) is honored even as it is transcended; the mature posture toward a thing fulfilled is honor, not contempt; remember where you came from]→ 25:4 (3 Ne 15:4-5; Gal 3:24; Matt 5:17; Ex 19:18)
- `doctrine:Elijah-turns-the-hearts-of-the-generations-lest-the-earth-be-cursed` —["I will send you Elijah the prophet before the coming of the great and dreadful day... he shall turn the heart of the fathers to the children, and the heart of the children to their fathers, lest I come and smite the earth with a curse"; the sealing power restored in Kirtland April 3 1836 (D&C 110:13-16), Moroni's first words to Joseph (D&C 2); the welding of the family chain across death; the staggering "why" — without the turning of hearts the WHOLE earth would be smitten/utterly wasted, so the family bond across death is load-bearing for the earth's entire purpose]→ 25:5-6 (D&C 110:13-16; D&C 2; JS-H 1:38-39; D&C 138:47-48)
- `theme:the-last-word-of-the-prophets-is-family-not-wrath` —[Malachi 4 is "The End of the Prophets" — the final words of the OT prophets, and Christ gives them to the Nephites as the close of the record He's been completing; the last note of the old covenant is not judgment but family — hearts turning between generations, the earth spared because love reaches across death; the Book of Mormon is itself Elijah's work in book form — Mormon to us, the fathers' words preserved for the children, hearts turned across time]→ 25:6 (Mal 4:6; 3 Ne 23:6-13; 3 Ne 24:16; W of M 1:1-11)

### from 3 Nephi 26
- `doctrine:Christ-expounds-all-things-from-the-beginning-to-the-last-day` —[Christ "did expound all things... both great and small," "from the beginning until the time that he should come in his glory... even until the elements should melt with fervent heat, and the earth should be wrapt together as a scroll," to "the great and last day" of judgment (good→resurrection of life, evil→resurrection of damnation, by mercy/justice/holiness); the whole cosmic arc — creation to consummation — taught in three days by "Christ, who was before the world began"; He expounds history not as a scholar reconstructs it but as its Author, from before its first page]→ 26:1-5 (3 Ne 1:14; Ether 3:14; 2 Pet 3:10; Dan 12:2; Mosiah 16:10-11)
- `doctrine:the-record-is-given-for-future-generations-by-the-Fathers-command` —["These scriptures, which ye had not with you, the Father commanded that I should give unto you; for it was wisdom in him that they should be given unto future generations"; the Malachi chapters given not primarily for the hearers but for us — the Father building the record deliberately with future readers in view; third chapter running on Christ tending the record (audit 23, supply 24-25), motive now named: the care taken with the record is care taken with us]→ 26:2 (3 Ne 23:6-13; 1 Ne 9:5; W of M 1:7; 2 Ne 27:6-22)
- `doctrine:the-lesser-part-is-given-first-to-try-faith-belief-unlocks-the-greater` —[Christ taught all things, Mormon preserves "a hundredth part" — not lost but withheld: "the Lord forbade it, saying: I will try the faith of my people"; the lesser given first "to try their faith," and "if they shall believe these things then shall the greater things be made manifest... if they will not believe... then shall the greater things be withheld, unto their condemnation"; belief in the lesser is the KEY to the greater — the same law as 2 Ne 28:30 / Matt 13:12 / Alma 12:9; the gaps are design, not accident; the person who says "show me the greater and I'll believe" has it backwards; the Book of Mormon in our hands IS the entrance exam for the sealed portion (Ether 4:7)]→ 26:6-11 (2 Ne 28:30; Matt 13:12; Alma 12:9-11; Ether 4:7; D&C 6:26-27; John 21:25)
- `doctrine:out-of-the-mouth-of-babes-the-children-become-revelators` —[the greater things withheld from the believing ADULTS flowed freely through the children — Christ "did loose their tongues, and they did speak unto their fathers great and marvelous things, even greater than he had revealed unto the people"; the babes "utter marvelous things," forbidden to be written; the same children He'd encircled with fire and wept over (3 Ne 17) are now the revelators — the least become the channel of the greatest, "out of the mouth of babes" made literal; the fathers told the greater would be withheld until their faith proved out hear it anyway, from the mouths of their own babes — mercy finds a way around the test even as the test stands]→ 26:14, 16 (Matt 11:25; 3 Ne 17:11-24; 3 Ne 11:37-38; Matt 18:3)
- `theme:unspeakable-things-not-lawful-to-be-written` —["many of them saw and heard unspeakable things, which are not lawful to be written"; Paul's experience exactly (2 Cor 12:4, "unspeakable words, which it is not lawful for a man to utter"); a category of the sacred not for the page — not conspiratorially secret but given to be lived, not transcribed; even the carefully-tended record has an edge it does not cross — a perfect record-keeper writes only what is lawful to write]→ 26:18 (2 Cor 12:4; 3 Ne 17:17; D&C 76:115-116; 3 Ne 27:23)
- `doctrine:the-church-of-Christ-established-baptism-Holy-Ghost-all-things-common` —[the hinge from Christ's three-day ministry to the institution: disciples baptize and teach, "as many as were baptized in the name of Jesus were filled with the Holy Ghost," "they had all things common among them, every man dealing justly," "did do all things even as Jesus had commanded them," and "were called the church of Christ"; the church built on baptism, the Spirit, consecration, justice, and His name; "all things common" is the seed of 4 Nephi's golden age — the marvelous made daily; a people who saw the heavens opened come down and deal justly and hold all things common — that is what the revelation was FOR]→ 26:17-21 (4 Ne 1:1-3; Acts 2:44-45; Moses 7:18; Mosiah 18:17; 3 Ne 27:3-8)

### from 3 Nephi 27
- `doctrine:the-church-must-bear-Christs-name-AND-be-built-on-his-gospel` —["how be it my church save it be called in my name?... if it be called in my name then it is my church, IF it so be that they are built upon my gospel"; two requirements, the conditional carrying the weight — the name is necessary (a church named for a man is that man's church) but not sufficient; a church can wear the right name and not be His if built "upon the works of men, or upon the works of the devil" → "joy in their works for a season" then "hewn down and cast into the fire"; the name without the gospel is a label on the wrong building; this is why Christ immediately defines the gospel — He's just made it the load-bearing test]→ 27:5-12 (D&C 115:4; 1 Cor 1:12-13; Mosiah 5:8-12; Alma 5:38)
- `doctrine:the-gospel-defined-by-Christ-himself` —[the single clearest definition of "the gospel" in scripture: "I came into the world to do the will of my Father... that I might be lifted up upon the cross... that I might draw all men unto me... to be judged of their works"; divine side = the Father sent the Son to be lifted up to draw all men; human side = "repent... be baptized in my name, that ye may be sanctified by the reception of the Holy Ghost, that ye may stand spotless"; faith→repentance→baptism→sanctification by the Spirit→endure→spotless; the doctrine of Christ of 2 Ne 31 spoken by Christ Himself; the gospel is not everything religious but THIS specific atoning mission + prescribed response]→ 27:13-21 (2 Ne 31:10-21; 3 Ne 11:31-41; John 12:32; D&C 76:40-42)
- `image:washed-their-garments-in-my-blood` —["no unclean thing can enter into his kingdom... save it be those who have washed their garments in my blood, because of their faith, and the repentance of all their sins, and their faithfulness unto the end"; a deliberate paradox — blood stains, only Christ's blood cleanses (Rev 7:14, robes made white in the blood of the Lamb); the impossibility (no unclean thing) and the provision (washed in His blood) stated in the same breath — hopeless except for whose blood it is; the blood cleanses, faith/repentance/faithfulness are how one comes to be washed in it]→ 27:19 (Rev 7:14; 1 Ne 12:10; Alma 5:21-27; Alma 13:11-13)
- `doctrine:what-manner-of-men-ought-ye-to-be-even-as-I-am` —[the verse that holds the chapter — to men about to judge others, Christ asks "what manner of men ought ye to be?" and answers with the highest answer there is: "even as I am"; not "be good men" or "be better than those you judge" but BE AS I AM; the Sermon's "be ye therefore perfect" (3 Ne 12:48) sharpened to the first person; the whole gospel just defined (faith→repentance→baptism→sanctification) has THIS as its destination — not merely forgiven or admitted but made like Him; the standard is both impossibly high and, through the gospel, actually attainable — the end the sanctifying Spirit is FOR]→ 27:27 (Matt 5:48; 3 Ne 12:48; Moro 7:48; 1 John 3:2; 2 Pet 1:4)
- `doctrine:out-of-the-books-shall-the-world-be-judged` —["Write the things which ye have seen and heard... out of the books which have been written, and which shall be written, shall this people be judged... all things are written by the Father; therefore out of the books which shall be written shall the world be judged"; the fourth chapter running on the record — Christ audited it (23), supplied it (24-25), explained its purpose (26), now states its ultimate function: JUDGMENT; two records converge — the earthly books the disciples write + "all things written by the Father" (the heavenly book of life/remembrance, 24:16); this is why Christ has been so exacting about the record — it is the very basis on which the world will be judged]→ 27:23-26 (2 Ne 33:10-15; W of M 1:11; 3 Ne 24:16; Rev 20:12)
- `theme:Christ-has-fulness-of-joy-and-real-sorrow-at-once` —["my joy is great, even unto fulness, because of you, and also this generation... none of them are lost" — then immediately "it sorroweth me because of the fourth generation... they will sell me for silver and for gold"; the Savior who wept over the children (3 Ne 17) here declares His joy FULL over this generation and grieves the apostasy four generations out, in two breaths; His perfect foreknowledge does not anesthetize His feeling — He knows exactly what is coming and grieves it anyway (Gen 6:6, God "was grieved"); joy over those who receive Him, grief over those who reject Him, both real, both at once]→ 27:30-32 (John 17:12; 3 Ne 17:14; Gen 6:6; Moses 7:28-29)
- `theme:enter-at-the-strait-gate-while-it-is-day` —["Enter ye in at the strait gate... narrow is the way that leads to life, and few there be that find it... until the night cometh, wherein no man can work"; the Sermon's narrow way (3 Ne 14:13-14) joined to the urgency of John 9:4 — work while it is day; after the fulness of joy and the foreseen sorrow, the closing word is: choose the narrow way NOW, while there is still light to work in]→ 27:33 (Matt 7:13-14; 3 Ne 14:13-14; John 9:4; Alma 34:32-33)

### from 3 Nephi 28
- `doctrine:the-question-of-the-hearts-desire-reveals-the-soul` —[Christ asks each disciple individually "What is it that ye desire of me, after that I am gone to the Father?" — the question He asked Solomon (2 Chr 1:7) and will ask in D&C 7; what each answers exposes the shape of his heart, more than any test of works; nine ask for rest and speedy reunion (granted at 72), three durst not speak that they desired to tarry; the heart's desire is the truest revelation of the soul]→ 28:1-9 (2 Chr 1:7-12; D&C 7:1-8; 1 Kgs 3:5; John 21:22)
- `doctrine:the-more-blessed-desire-is-to-keep-bringing-souls-not-to-rest-sooner` —["more blessed are ye... ye have desired that ye might bring the souls of men unto me, while the world shall stand"; not a ranking of the disciples (the nine fully blessed) but of the DIRECTION of desire — the nine wanted rest, the three wanted more labor; the "more blessed" is the consecrating impulse that asks not "when may I rest?" but "how long may I serve?", wanting to give more rather than receive sooner; the same shape as the Savior's own ministry, who could have come down and did not]→ 28:7-9 (3 Ne 27:32; Phil 1:23-24; John 9:4; Mosiah 2:17)
- `doctrine:the-chain-of-oneness-disciple-as-Christ-Christ-as-Father-Father-and-Son-one` —["ye shall be even as I am, and I am even as the Father; and the Father and I are one; and the Holy Ghost beareth record of the Father and me"; the becoming of 27:27 extended to full theology — the path of the disciple runs INTO the oneness of the Godhead; double work: a statement of the Godhead's unity ("the Father and I are one," cf. 3 Ne 11:27, 2 Ne 31:21) AND of the disciple's incorporation into it ("ye shall be even as I am"); the oneness is real and shared, not a collapse of persons — the Holy Ghost "beareth record of the Father and me," distinguishing them even in unity; major datapoint for is-jesus-christ-god]→ 28:10-11 (3 Ne 11:27; 2 Ne 31:21; John 17:21-23; Morm 7:7)
- `doctrine:transfiguration-is-the-enabling-condition-of-beholding-God` —["it did seem unto them like a transfiguration of them, that they were changed from this body of flesh into an immortal state, that they could behold the things of God"; the same necessity Moses described (Moses 1:11, "his glory was upon me... I was transfigured before him... no man can behold all the glory of God and afterwards remain in the flesh"); the transfiguration is not a reward but the enabling CONDITION of seeing God and surviving it — a mortal body must be changed, even temporarily, to behold the things of God]→ 28:15 (Moses 1:11; Matt 17:1-2; 3 Ne 19:25; D&C 67:11)
- `theme:the-OT-deliverance-types-multiplied-in-the-three-Nephites` —[the deliverances allude deliberately to the OT's great types — "thrice they were cast into a furnace and received no harm" (Shadrach/Meshach/Abednego, Dan 3); "twice... cast into a den of wild beasts; and behold they did play with the beasts as a child with a suckling lamb" (Daniel in the lions' den, Dan 6); prisons "rent in twain" (Acts 16:26); the furnace and the lions' den, the two iconic images of God preserving His servants intact, gathered up and multiplied; playing with beasts reaches forward to Isaiah's peaceable kingdom (Isa 11:6) — the three already live in a body the last day will give everyone]→ 28:19-22 (Dan 3:25; Dan 6:16-27; Acts 16:26; Isa 11:6)
- `theme:Mormon-models-the-honest-record-I-know-not-then-I-have-inquired` —[Mormon writes honestly "whether they were mortal or immortal... I know not" (v17) — does not pretend to knowledge he lacks, marks the uncertainty IN the record; then (vv36-37) "since I wrote, I have inquired of the Lord, and he hath made it manifest unto me" — didn't leave the gap, inquired, got the answer, transparently updated showing the seam; exactly the posture ch 23 dramatized (a found gap acknowledged, filled by inquiry, correction shown not hidden); a prophet modeling intellectual + spiritual honesty in the text — say what you don't know, ask, correct openly; the same standard read-before-quoting runs on]→ 28:17, 36-37 (3 Ne 23:6-13; 3 Ne 26:11; W of M 1:11; D&C 9:7-9)
- `doctrine:the-doctrine-of-translation-sanctified-in-the-flesh-but-not-yet-resurrected` —[the change wrought on the three: "that they might not taste of death... might not suffer pain nor sorrow save it were for the sins of the world" (the one retained sorrow is the holy one, grief over sin, cf. 27:32); "Satan could have no power over them, that he could not tempt them; and they were sanctified in the flesh, that they were holy"; BUT "this change was not equal to that which shall take place at the last day" — translation is NOT resurrection but an intermediate sanctified state, still awaiting "a greater change" at judgment day to "go no more out"; the BoM does not blur translation into resurrection — names it its own category; even the most exalted mortal condition still looks forward to the final change]→ 28:38-40 (D&C 7:1-3; 3 Ne 19:25; 3 Ne 27:32; 4 Ne 1:14)

### from 3 Nephi 29
- `doctrine:the-coming-forth-of-the-record-is-the-sign-the-covenant-is-fulfilling` —["when these sayings shall come unto the Gentiles according to his word, then ye may know that the covenant which the Father hath made with the children of Israel, concerning their restoration... is already beginning to be fulfilled"; the Book of Mormon's coming-forth is ITSELF the sign that the gathering has begun — not just a message about the covenant but the covenant going into motion; the prophecy of its coming-forth (2 Ne 30, 27) was fulfilled, and a fulfilled prophecy is a witness (3 Ne 23) — so the existence of the book argues for the truth of the book; to hold it is to hold the proof God has begun to keep His ancient promise]→ 29:1-3 (2 Ne 30:3-8; 2 Ne 27; Morm 3:17; 5:14)
- `doctrine:wo-to-cessationism-God-who-changes-not-still-works-by-revelation-and-gifts` —["wo unto him that shall deny the revelations of the Lord, and that shall say the Lord no longer worketh by revelation, or by prophecy, or by gifts, or by tongues, or by healings, or by the power of the Holy Ghost!"; Mormon names cessationism in advance — the belief that the age of revelation/miracles/gifts has closed; treated as one of the gravest latter-day errors (with Morm 9, Moro 7) because it makes God a CHANGED God, and an unchanging God (Mal 3:6 / 3 Ne 24:6) cannot have stopped doing what He always did; the Restoration's whole foundation is the reversal of this denial — the heavens are NOT closed, God DOES still speak, the gifts HAVE returned]→ 29:5-6 (Morm 9:7-26; Moro 7:35-37; 2 Ne 28:4-6; Mal 3:6)
- `doctrine:denying-miracles-to-get-gain-is-priestcraft-likened-to-the-son-of-perdition` —["wo unto him that shall say at that day, TO GET GAIN, that there can be no miracle wrought by Jesus Christ; for he that doeth this shall become like unto the son of perdition, for whom there was no mercy"; the denial of miracles tied to priestcraft — a domesticated God safely confined to the past makes no present demands and is easier to package and sell; to deny the living miracle-working Christ for profit is the harshest comparison available (son of perdition), reserved not for the honest doubter but for the calculated, profitable denial of what one has reason to know is true]→ 29:7 (2 Ne 26:29-31; Morm 8:26-33; 2 Ne 9:9; 3 Ne 27:32)
- `doctrine:do-not-mock-the-Jews-or-Israel-the-covenant-stands` —["ye need not any longer hiss, nor spurn, nor make game of the Jews, nor any of the remnant of the house of Israel; for behold, the Lord remembereth his covenant unto them"; a Nephite prophet (~AD 385) warns the Gentile reader against CONTEMPT for the Jews — almost unbearably prescient given the centuries of Christian contempt and persecution that would follow; the ground is not tolerance-as-value but the COVENANT — the Jews and scattered remnant are not cast off; to mock them is to set oneself against the very thing the book's coming-forth signals is beginning]→ 29:8 (1 Ne 19:14; 2 Ne 29:4-5; Rom 11:1-2, 25-29; Zech 2:8)
- `doctrine:no-one-can-turn-the-Lords-right-hand-the-covenant-is-irreversible` —["ye need not suppose that ye can turn the right hand of the Lord unto the left, that he may not execute judgment unto the fulfilling of the covenant which he hath made unto the house of Israel"; no human contempt, no Gentile presumption, can deflect God's right hand from keeping His word to Israel; the covenant WILL be fulfilled; the only question for the Gentile reader is whether they stand with it or against it]→ 29:9 (Isa 14:27; Dan 4:35; 3 Ne 20:20; Ezek 20:37)
- `theme:the-record-proves-God-has-not-stopped-acting-speaking-or-covenant-keeping` —[the three warnings unified — each is a form of saying "God has stopped": the Lord delays His coming (stopped ACTING), He no longer works by revelation/miracles (stopped SPEAKING), the Jews are cast off (stopped COVENANT-KEEPING); the coming-forth of the book refutes all three at once because it is the living evidence God has NOT stopped — acting, speaking, and keeping covenant in the very fact of the record arriving in the reader's hands; Mormon's whole exhortation: the thing you hold proves God has not stopped — do not live or teach or sneer as though He had]→ 29:1-9 (Mal 3:6; Morm 9:9-11; Heb 13:8; 2 Ne 29:7-9)

### from 3 Nephi 30
- `doctrine:the-last-word-of-3-Nephi-is-invitation-not-condemnation` —[after the woes of ch 29 (spurning, denying revelation, mocking the Jews), the book ends on the OPEN DOOR — "come unto me"; the sequence matters: warning first, invitation last, the invitation where it rests; a God who only warned would be a God to fear, a God who only invited without naming sin wouldn't take it seriously — ch 29 names the seriousness, ch 30 opens the door anyway; the honest catalog of sins not softened (a mirror to the latter-day world) but followed immediately by the unconditional reach ("all ye Gentiles") and complete remedy]→ 30:1-2 (3 Ne 29:5-9; 3 Ne 27:20; 3 Ne 9:13-14; Alma 5:33-34)
- `doctrine:the-Gentile-who-comes-to-Christ-is-numbered-with-Israel` —["come unto me, and be baptized in my name... that ye may be numbered with my people who are of the house of Israel"; the grafting-in (Rom 11, Gal 3:29 "if ye be Christ's, then are ye Abraham's seed"); the Gentile who comes is not merely forgiven as an outsider but ADOPTED into Israel, made heir of the Abrahamic promise (Abr 2:10); the destination of the invitation is incorporation into the covenant people]→ 30:2 (Rom 11:17-24; Gal 3:27-29; 2 Ne 10:18-19; Abr 2:10)
